B006JJBFK0|5.0|With this release, Xandria have established themselves as hard-hitters on the front line of the symphonic metal genre. Neverworld's End is a varied album with the absolute highest musicianship and not a weak point or a hint of filler (of course, you wouldn't expect filler from an album five years in the making!). The band shows a major shift in composition and lyrics here compared to their previous albums, at least in part due to the departure of former vocalist and co-lyricist Lisa Middelhauve. I enjoy Xandria's former work, which was often quite relaxing as far as metal goes, but I prefer the hard-hitting edge of Neverworld's End (primarily composed by founder and guitarist/keyboardist Marco Hebaum), with the debut of Xandria's sublimely talented and versatile new vocalist Manuela Kraller. As I mentioned, the album contains a variety of song styles, from aggressive headbangers (Soulcrusher, Blood on my Hands, Cursed) to ballads (Forevermore, The Dream is Still Alive, A Thousand Letters) to exotic epics (A Prophecy of Worlds to Fall, The Nomad's Crown), each song distinct and complex on its own. The album is a coherent musical journey: there are several motifs that pop up throughout the album, and the speed and bombast wax and wane so as to keep you engaged but not exhuasted. Unlike many other bands, they don't abuse the `symphonic' part of symphonic metal; instead of drowning themselves out with bombast, Xandria uses orchestral parts primarily to follow and accent the band's melodies, the orchestra taking a backseat to the bands' stellar instrumentation. I don't think I can overstate how refreshing that is! I also like that the orchestration often performs well-composed Celtic or Middle Eastern/Indian melodies (such as in The Call of the Wind and The Nomad's Crown), a Xandria signature.<br /><br />Everybody and their dog has already pointed out that Manuela sounds similar to the superlative Tarja Turunen. Like Tarja, Manu is a heavy soprano (in terms of vocal weight, not body size :-P) with a dark timbre, wide range, high tessitura, and classical training. Still, I disagree with those who dismiss her as a clone, since her voice is deeper and has a breathier, throatier quality than Tarja's; I find the differences in their voices more pronounced the more I listen to Neverworld's End. I think a dramatic voice like Manu's is especially well-suited to heavy metal, sounding like another instrument in the band. I like Lisa as well, and actually find that when Manu sings softly in her lower register, she sounds rather similar to the way Lisa does in songs like Eversleeping (Ravenheart album).<br /><br />Neverworld's End sets a standard for the symphonic metal genre the way that Oceanborn did in Nightwish's glory days. The album is evocative of Tarja-era Nightwish in terms of depth, complexity, and musicianship, which Lisa (wife of bassist Nils Middelhauve) has said was one of Xandria's goals. However, I find a persistent power metal element in Neverworld's End that has been absent from Nightwish's work since Wishmaster. Some may denounce the supposed lack of originality, but as far as I'm concerned, Neverworld's End is superb in every way and heck, I've really missed this kind of epic effing METAL since Nightwish's Once, so I'm not complaining :-). Please, Xandria, continue bringing the awesome!

This the starting point for Andrew Goodman's book- one issue which has clearly emerged from the first decade of the CPR and that is that there's a greater possibility of judicial pre-determination of pre-trial opinion which is likely to influence the outcome of final proceedings.<br /><br />And it will depend now on whether the written material is of a high enough quality from a skeleton argument or opening note for the court or tribunal proceedings... whether we like it or not!<br /><br />Goodman has produced a first class practical guide to modern written advocacy here taking on board the lessons we've learnt from the way in which the CPR has taken us... at least as far as the final proceedings are concerned and how we prepare the case.<br /><br />It all starts with how competently the witness statements have been drafted to follow the Particulars or Defence, and it has become the practice in many courts and tribunals that heavy reliance and emphasis is placed on the written word- probably much more so than before.<br /><br />The beauty of Goodman's new edition of `Effective Written Advocacy' lies with the working examples from leading current advocates so we know what it is that the judges want.<br /><br />And before there are howls of criticism, can we say that it's probably the best way forward to enable the best formed opinion to be made and to save a great deal of time avoiding irrelevance.<br /><br />The book is an advocate's bible both invaluable and compelling and illustrates just how far the role of the advocate has matured with the development of the CPR in the last decade as the practice books and supplements expand worryingly every year.<br /><br />The teaching of advocacy in the 1970s and 1980s was considered poor.  The re-structured Bar Vocational Course (as it then was) attempted to sort this out in the early 1990s but it was very apparent to the Judiciary that the competency levels of written and oral advocacy remained lamentably low, so the criticisms remained and there have been improvements.<br /><br />Now, thankfully, the direction Goodman has taken us in with this book is to be welcomed for the commonsense given throughout. Effective written advocacy is all about the use of intelligence, or attention to detail to use a less controversial word.<br /><br />You, the advocate, must know the sort of answers to the questions you ask, but to be one step ahead at the beginning before the face to face stuff starts the written word rules. The authors have broken with the more usual approach to teaching jurisprudence which is to be welcomed for its innovative study method deployed here.<br /><br />New editions for Jurisprudence do not appear as frequently as, say `case heavy' substantive law areas so the authors have merely tinkered with the text to improve it and sharpen it for the new edition... and they do just that! So this second edition includes a rearrangement of the general sections, re-written where necessary for a more systematic coverage.<br /><br />With the advanced sections some new topics have been added, notably on law and deconstruction, and law and autopoiesis to name just a couple of areas. There's also an enhanced discussion of the rise of legal positivism linked to the rise of the modern state. The changing role of natural and human rights discourse is well covered to take account of recent developments.<br /><br />Professors Veitch, Christodoulidis and Farmer have created a very modern teaching tool here breaking from the old approaches so the book is very well described as `accessible, interdisciplinary and socially informed' and successfully takes account of the most recent developments in current jurisprudential thought. B00001OH7O|5.0|1971, it seems hard to imagine anyone would have predicted that Bowie would follow up THE MAN WHO SOLD THE WORLD with his third album, HUNK DORY.  Where THE MAN WHO SOLD THE WORLD depicted Bowie moving in a harder, rockier direction, HUNKY DORY is different in so many ways.  Mick Ronson's stellar guitar work is turned down in the mix in favor for Rick Wakeman's fantastic piano.  The real highlight of the album, however, is Bowie's knack for melody.  While the previous two albums were good, HUNKY DORY really established Bowie as something other than a one-hit wonder.<br /><br />The album begins with \\"Changes.\\"  It's a song that may feel overplayed today, appearing in many commercials, but in the context of this record, it is an unbelievably well-written pop song.  The lyrics describe a man who changes his life so that no one will ever be able to pin him down.  This early in his career, Bowie gives the world his modus operandi, a pattern that would be replicated with Ziggy Stardust, Halloween Jack, and the Thin White Duke.  \\"Life on Mars\\" assures the listener that this isn't just another vapid pop album; it's a song that is rich in instrumentation and lyrical content.  Rick Wakeman's piano is brought to the forefront in the song along with Bowie's belted chorus and sweeping strings.  The song concludes with one of Ronson's spacey-rock guitar solos before giving way to bombarding cellos.  The arrangement early in HUNKY DORY focuses on piano-based pop.  As the album wears on, the piano slowly fades out in favor for most guitar work, starting noticeably with the thick, deep acoustics of \\"Quicksand.\\"  By the time the rocking, proto-punk \\"Queen Bitch\\" appears on the album, the piano is buried in the mix; this transition feels seamless.  A fan favorite, \\"Queen Bitch\\" is a rocking, glam-rock anthem.  Dripping with attitude, it would foreshadow Bowie's work on THE RISE AND FALL OF ZIGGY STARDUST AND THE SPIDERS FROM MARS.  It's hard to believe that only a few tracks ago, the same songwriter was performing \\"Kooks,\\" a song that wouldn't sound out of place in a Broadway musical.<br /><br />HUNKY DORY ends with \\"The Bewlay Brothers.\\"  Bowie was once quoted saying that Americans would love this song, as per their constant need to search for meaning in lyrics.  He was right; the lyrics here are chilling and cryptic.  Often speculated to be about this schizophrenic half-brother Terry, the eerie song never loses its sharp melody.  It's a sour note to end a mostly uptempo and uplifting album.<br /><br />While ZIGGY STARDUST is often regarded as Bowie's undisputed masterpiece, HUNKY DORY nearly usurps it.  It's just as good as ZIGGY, and in many respects, better.  This is an essential album for rock fans, especially those interested in rock music from the 1970's.  Standout songs for sampling/downloading: \\"Changes,\\" \\"Oh! You Pretty Things,\\" \\"Life on Mars,\\" \\"Queen Bitch.\\"  This is a remarkably consistent album that deserves to be poured over.same songwriter was performing \\"Kooks,\\" a song that wouldn't sound out of place in a Broadway musical.<br /><br />HUNKY DORY ends with \\"The Bewlay Brothers.\\"  Bowie was once quoted saying that Americans would love this song, as per their constant need to search for meaning in lyrics. B00001OH7P|5.0|It would be hard to say anything about THE RISE AND FALL OF ZIGGY STARDUST AND THE SPIDERS FROM MARS that hasn't been said already.  Most of what you've heard is true:  it's a concept album about an alien creature that visits Earth in an attempt to save it (and humanity) from itself. To follow this up, instead of revisiting that same creative process, Bowie created an alter ego to create his next album.  A risky move to be sure, but one that would soon pay dividends.  ZIGGY STARDUST is 11 songs of fantastic rock-n-roll.  It earns its \\"Glam\\" title primarily for the approach that Bowie took for it (costumes, theatricality, etc...), but make no mistake, there's just as much substance here as there is style.<br /><br />ZIGGY STARDUST begins with the amazing \\"Five Years.\\"  The song tells a story of a young man who discovers the end of the world has been announced. Instead of blatantly stealing, Bowie has repurposed this chorus.  The fact that it IS \\"Somewhere Over the Rainbow\\" is significant to the lyrical content of the song.<br /><br />The album ends with the 1-2-3 punch of \\"Ziggy Stardust,\\" \\"Suffragette City,\\" and \\"Rock & Roll Suicide.\\"  If the first 8 songs recount the \\"rise\\" of Ziggy Stardust, these last three surely document his \\"fall.\\"  In \\"Ziggy Stardust,\\" the protagonist loses sight of his mission and gives in to fame, women, and drugs.  \\"Suffragette City\\" follows him as he objectifies women.  The chilling \\"Rock & Roll Suicide\\" concludes the album, notorious for being the final song before Bowie \\"killed Ziggy\\" on stage in concert.  The song follows Ziggy, a washed up, alienated rock star who turns to drugs as he completely gives up: \\"Just turn on with me, and you're not alone!\\"  Similar to the pleading repeated refrain of \\"Five Years,\\" we are left with Ziggy's final thoughts to end the album.  It's a sour note to end on, but one that is both horrifying and completely satisfying.  One thing to note: I may have focused on the lyrics here, but I must stress, these songs are fantastic: packed with great guitar-work, killer melodies, and vivid imagery.<br /><br />THE RISE AND FALL OF ZIGGY STARDUST AND THE SPIDERS FROM MARS is probably remembered most for its eponymous hero.  It's important to not lose sight of the fact that this album is a fantastic, creative piece of work.  40-years later, it feels just as creative and original as it ever did.  For fans of Bowie, this album is not optional -- it's essential listening.  For casual music listeners, this album is packed with great songs to keep you interested.  This is album is absolute classic on par with SGT PEPPERS or EXILE ON MAINSTREET; everyone should listen to this sometime in their life. In 2012, another remastered version of this album was also released. No matter the style of the work, the tracks are concise, brief, and consistent.  \\"Missing Pieces\\" begins the album, with a shy keyboard intro before launching into White's trademark vocals and guitar.  The next song, \\"Sixteen Saltines,\\" drips with the attitude and timbre that brought the White Stripes to the mainstream consciousness.  Most of the songs here are 3-minutes or less, but this record never feels short or unfulfilling. It all ends with \\"Take Me With You When You Go.\\"  It's a song that, in little over 4 minutes, sums up the entire album: a fitting and enjoyable way to end a great album.<br /><br />This album is a great addition to Jack White's already stellar catalog.  BLUNDERBUSS simultaneously sums up and adds to the songwriters' career. In this case, I think foolish mistakes were made probably because the director wanted to make his mark and satisfy his ego.  The result is a watchable and even enjoyable film which could easily have been much better.<br /><br />This version is actually less true to the book than the 80's version. Well, Jane Austen put it there as a crucial proof of Catherine's character at this stage of the book or movie.  Stupidly left out...  Also left out is the full characterization of Tilney and Catherine- all they had to do is follow Jane Austen's lead as the 80's version did... instead they truncated the dialogue- again very dumb especially unforgivable because they had the 80's version to look at and recognize how important it is to the integrity of the story.<br /><br />What this version does do better than the 80's version is the casting of Felicity Jones as Catherine, someone Henry Tilney would find extremely attractive both physically and for her simplicity and integrity- she is quite perfect.
